(kubernetes/kubernetes)\\n\\nKubernetes implements a sophisticated health checking system with three distinct endpoints:\\n\\n**Endpoints:** `/healthz`, `/livez`, `/readyz`\\n\\n**Key Files:**\\n- state\\n\\n**Architecture:**\\nKubernetes uses a health check registry pattern where multiple checks are collected and installed via `InstallPathHandler()`. The system supports excluding checks via query parameters (`?exclude=check-name`) and verbose output (`?verbose=1`). Each registry (healthz, livez, readyz) maintains independent check lists with optional grace periods for livez during boot sequences.\\n\\n### Grafana (grafana/grafana)\\n\\nGrafana implements a minimal health endpoint system focused on operator readiness signaling.\\n\\n**Endpoints:** `/livez`, `/readyz`\\n\\n**Key Files:**\\n- `pkg/server/health.go` - Health endpoint handlers and HealthNotifier state management\\n- `pkg/services/apiserver/service.go` - Endpoint registration via gorilla/mux\\n\\n**Key Symbols:**\\n- `HealthNotifier` struct - Thread-safe state holder using `atomic.Bool`\\n- `LivezHandler()` - Always returns 200 OK (process is alive)\\n- `ReadyzHandler(h *HealthNotifier)` - Returns 200 OK if ready, 503 if not ready\\n- `RegisterHealthEndpoints()` - Registers both endpoints on provided router\\n- `SetReady()`, `SetNotReady()`, `IsReady()` - State management methods\\n\\n**Dependency Checks:**\\nGrafana uses a simple binary readiness state managed by operators. No automatic dependency checks for databases or caches. Instead, operators explicitly signal readiness via `SetReady()` after completing initialization.\\n\\n**Architecture:**\\nGrafana's approach is intentionally simple: livez always succeeds (indicating the HTTP server is running), while readyz returns success only when the operator has explicitly called `SetReady()`. This allows operators to perform their own initialization checks and signal completion. The health state is shared across the InstrumentationServer and OperatorServer via a single shared `HealthNotifier` instance.\\n\\n### Prometheus (prometheus/prometheus)\\n\\nPrometheus implements health endpoints with TSDB readiness gating and graceful shutdown support.\\n\\n**Endpoints:** `/-/healthy`, `/-/ready` (note: different path prefix convention)\\n\\n**Key Files:**\\n- `web/web.go` - Handler definition, ReadyStatus state machine, and endpoint registration\\n\\n**Key Symbols:**\\n- `ReadyStatus` enum with three states: `NotReady` (iota = 0), `Ready` (= 1), `Stopping` (= 2)\\n- `testReady()` method - Wraps handlers with readiness checks\\n- `isReady()` - Returns true if ReadyStatus == Ready\\n- `setReady()`, `setNotReady()`, `setStopping()` - State transition methods\\n- Metrics: `prometheus_ready` gauge tracks readiness state\\n\\n**Dependency Checks:**\\n- **TSDB Readiness:** The ready endpoint checks if TSDB (Time Series Database) has completed initialization\\n- **Graceful Shutdown:** Returns 503 when in Stopping state (signaling removal from load balancers while keeping liveness checks passing)\\n\\n**Architecture:**\\nPrometheus uses a state machine approach with three states. The `/-/healthy` endpoint (HEAD and GET support) always succeeds, while `/-/ready` (also HEAD and GET) wraps handlers with `testReady()` middleware that:\\n- Returns 200 OK if Ready\\n- Returns 503 Service Unavailable with `X-Prometheus-Stopping: false` if NotReady\\n- Returns 503 Service Unavailable with `X-Prometheus-Stopping: true` if Stopping\\n\\nThis allows clients to distinguish between \\\"not yet ready\\\" and \\\"actively shutting down\\\" scenarios. The ready endpoint also guards API endpoints like `/federate` and `/consoles` to prevent serving traffic during startup or shutdown.\\n\\n### Comparison Summary\\n\\n| Aspect | Kubernetes | Grafana | Prometheus |\\n|--------|-----------|---------|------------|\\n| **Endpoints** | /healthz, /livez, /readyz | /livez, /readyz | /-/healthy, /-/ready |\\n| **DB Checks** | Yes (etcd via NamedGroupedCheck) | No (manual) | Implicit (TSDB readiness) |\\n| **Cache/Informer Checks** | Yes (NewInformerSyncHealthz) | No | No |\\n| **Pluggable Checks** | Yes (HealthChecker interface) | No (binary state only) | No |\\n| **Shutdown Handling** | Explicit NewShutdownHealthz | No | Stopping state with header |\\n| **Grace Periods** | Yes (livez grace period) | No | No |\\n| **Query Parameters** | Yes (?exclude, ?verbose) | No | No |\\n\\n**Common Patterns:**\\n- All three separate liveness (/livez or /-/healthy) from readiness (/readyz or /-/ready)\\n- Readiness checks block traffic during startup\\n- Support for HTTP HEAD requests in addition to GET\\n- Graceful shutdown integration (explicit in Kubernetes/Prometheus, implicit in Grafana via SetNotReady)\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2047,"cache_read_input_tokens":75903,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2047},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"bdc1b489-b9fc-4bb1-99f3-e81f7106c356","uuid":"ebef89bf-f12d-45d7-96a8-2bbe0a0d8244"}

Projects\\n\\n### Kubernetes (kubernetes/kubernetes)\\n\\nKubernetes implements a sophisticated health checking system with three distinct endpoints:\\n\\n**Endpoints:** `/healthz`, `/livez`, `/readyz`\\n\\n**Key Files:**\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/healthz/healthz.go` - Core health check framework defining the `HealthChecker` interface with `Name()` and `Check(req `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/options/etcd.go` - Database-specific health checks\\n\\n**Key Symbols:**\\n- `InstallHandler()`, `InstallReadyzHandler()`, `InstallLivezHandler()` - Registration functions for endpoints\\n- `HealthChecker` interface - Pluggable health check implementation\\n- Built-in checks: `PingHealthz` (always returns ok), `LogHealthz` (verifies logging not blocked), `NewInformerSyncHealthz()` (checks informer cache sync), `NewShutdownHealthz()` (fails when shutdown starts)\\n\\n**Dependency Checks:**\\n- **Database (etcd):** `CreateHealthCheck()` and `CreateReadyCheck()` from storage factory check etcd connectivity and readiness via `NamedGroupedCheck(\\\"etcd-readiness\\\", \\\"etcd-readiness\\\", ...)`\\n- **Informers:** Verify all informers have synced caches\\n- **Shutdown Signal:** Track graceful shutdown state\\n\\n**Architecture:**\\nKubernetes uses a health check registry pattern where multiple checks are collected and installed via `InstallPathHandler()`. The system supports excluding checks via query parameters (`?exclude=check-name`) and verbose output (`?verbose=1`). Each registry (healthz, livez, readyz) maintains independent check lists with optional grace periods for livez during boot sequences.\\n\\n### Grafana (grafana/grafana)\\n\\nGrafana implements a minimal health endpoint system focused on operator readiness signaling.\\n\\n**Endpoints:** `/livez`, `/readyz`\\n\\n**Key Files:**\\n- `pkg/server/health.go` - Health endpoint handlers and HealthNotifier state management\\n- `pkg/services/apiserver/service.go` - Endpoint registration via gorilla/mux\\n\\n**Key Symbols:**\\n- `HealthNotifier` struct - Thread-safe state holder using `atomic.Bool`\\n- `LivezHandler()` - Always returns 200 OK (process is alive)\\n- `ReadyzHandler(h *HealthNotifier)` - Returns 200 OK if ready, 503 if not ready\\n- `RegisterHealthEndpoints()` - Registers both endpoints on provided router\\n- `SetReady()`, `SetNotReady()`, `IsReady()` - State management methods\\n\\n**Dependency Checks:**\\nGrafana uses a simple binary readiness state managed by operators. No automatic dependency checks for databases or caches. Instead, operators explicitly signal readiness via `SetReady()` after completing initialization.\\n\\n**Architecture:**\\nGrafana's approach is intentionally simple: livez always succeeds (indicating the HTTP server is running), while readyz returns success only when the operator has explicitly called `SetReady()`. This allows operators to perform their own initialization checks and signal completion. The health state is shared across the InstrumentationServer and OperatorServer via a single shared `HealthNotifier` instance.\\n\\n### Prometheus (prometheus/prometheus)\\n\\nPrometheus implements health endpoints with TSDB readiness gating and graceful shutdown support.\\n\\n**Endpoints:** `/-/healthy`, `/-/ready` (note: different path prefix convention)\\n\\n**Key Files:**\\n- `web/web.go` - Handler definition, ReadyStatus state machine, and endpoint registration\\n\\n**Key Symbols:**\\n- `ReadyStatus` enum with three states: `NotReady` (iota = 0), `Ready` (= 1), `Stopping` (= 2)\\n- `testReady()` method - Wraps handlers with readiness checks\\n- `isReady()` - Returns true if ReadyStatus == Ready\\n- `setReady()`, `setNotReady()`, `setStopping()` - State transition methods\\n- Metrics: `prometheus_ready` gauge tracks readiness state\\n\\n**Dependency Checks:**\\n- **TSDB Readiness:** The ready endpoint checks if TSDB (Time Series Database) has completed initialization\\n- **Graceful Shutdown:** Returns 503 when in Stopping state (signaling removal from load balancers while keeping liveness checks passing)\\n\\n**Architecture:**\\nPrometheus uses a state machine approach with three states. The `/-/healthy` endpoint (HEAD and GET support) always succeeds, while `/-/ready` (also HEAD and GET) wraps handlers with `testReady()` middleware that:\\n- Returns 200 OK if Ready\\n- Returns 503 Service Unavailable with `X-Prometheus-Stopping: false` if NotReady\\n- Returns 503 Service Unavailable with `X-Prometheus-Stopping: true` if Stopping\\n\\nThis allows clients to distinguish between \\\"not yet ready\\\" and \\\"actively shutting down\\\" scenarios. The ready endpoint also guards API endpoints like `/federate` and `/consoles` to prevent serving traffic during startup or shutdown.\\n\\n### Comparison Summary\\n\\n| Aspect | Kubernetes | Grafana | Prometheus |\\n|--------|-----------|---------|------------|\\n| **Endpoints** | /healthz, /livez, /readyz | /livez, /readyz | /-/healthy, /-/ready |\\n| **DB Checks** | Yes (etcd via NamedGroupedCheck) | No (manual) | Implicit (TSDB readiness) |\\n| **Cache/Informer Checks** | Yes (NewInformerSyncHealthz) | No | No |\\n| **Pluggable Checks** | Yes (HealthChecker interface) | No (binary state only) | No |\\n| **Shutdown Handling** | Explicit NewShutdownHealthz | No | Stopping state with header |\\n| **Grace Periods** | Yes (livez grace period) | No | No |\\n| **Query Parameters** | Yes (?exclude, ?verbose) | No | No |\\n\\n**Common Patterns:**\\n- All three separate liveness (/livez or /-/healthy) from readiness (/readyz or /-/ready)\\n- Readiness checks block traffic during startup\\n- Support for HTTP HEAD requests in addition to GET\\n- Graceful shutdown integration (explicit in Kubernetes/Prometheus, implicit in Grafana via SetNotReady)\"\n   172→}\n   173→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware.
